[21.03.19, 11:03:41] David Kn√∂rzer: public boolean search(String[] data, String target, int start, int end) {
        if (start > end) return false;
        else {
            int middle = (start + end) / 2;
            if (data[middle].equals(target)) return true;
            else if (data[middle].compareTo(target) < 0) {
                return search(data, target, middle + 1, end);
            } else return search(data, target, start, middle - 1);
        }
    }

import javafx.animation.PathTransition;
import javafx.application.Application;
import javafx.scene.Group;
import javafx.scene.Scene;
import javafx.scene.image.Image;
import javafx.scene.paint.Color;
import javafx.scene.paint.ImagePattern;
import javafx.scene.shape.*;
import javafx.stage.Stage;
import javafx.util.Duration;

import java.util.ArrayList;


public class DealAnimation extends Application {

    public void start(Stage dealStage) throws Exception {
        int player = 1;

        Group group =new Group();
        Path path = new Path();
        if(player==1){
        for(int i=0; player*5>i;i++) {
            Rectangle rect = new Rectangle(100, 150);
            rect.setArcHeight(15);
            rect.setArcWidth(15);
            rect.setStroke(Color.BLACK);
            Image testImage = new Image("/Sem2/Lecture_5/BackgroundRed.png");
            rect.setFill(new ImagePattern(testImage));


            LineTo line = new LineTo((100 * i) + 100, 100);
            MoveTo moveTo = new MoveTo(150, 800);
            path.getElements().add(moveTo);
            path.getElements().add(line);
            PathTransition transition = new PathTransition();
            transition.setDuration(Duration.seconds(0.5));
            transition.setNode(rect);
            transition.setPath(path);
            transition.setCycleCount(1);
            transition.setAutoReverse(false);
            group.getChildren().addAll(rect);

            transition.play();
        }

        }
        if(player==2){
            for(int i=0; player*5>i;i++) {

                rect.setArcWidth(15);

                group.getChildren().addAll(rect);



                transition.play();
            }

[28.03.19, 13:36:13] Philipp Yanni: package Sem2.Lecture_5;

import javafx.animation.RotateTransition;
import javafx.animation.ScaleTransition;
import javafx.application.Application;
import javafx.scene.Group;
import javafx.scene.Scene;
import javafx.scene.image.Image;
import javafx.scene.paint.Color;
import javafx.scene.paint.ImagePattern;
import javafx.scene.shape.Rectangle;
import javafx.stage.Stage;
import javafx.util.Duration;

public class FlipAnimation extends Application {

    public void start(Stage flipStage) throws Exception {


        Rectangle front = new Rectangle(100, 150);
        front.setArcHeight(15);
        front.setArcWidth(15);
        front.setStroke(Color.BLACK);
        Image testImage = new Image("/Sem2/Lecture_5/BackgroundRed.png");
        front.setFill(new ImagePattern(testImage));
        front.setY(200);

        Rectangle back = new Rectangle(100,150,Color.BLUE);
        front.setArcHeight(15);
        front.setArcWidth(15);
        front.setStroke(Color.BLACK);
        back.setY(200);
        back.setScaleX(0);

        ScaleTransition stHideFront = new ScaleTransition(Duration.seconds(0.5), front);
        stHideFront.setFromX(1);
        stHideFront.setToX(0);

        ScaleTransition stShowBack = new ScaleTransition(Duration.seconds(0.5), back);
        stShowBack.setFromX(0);
        stShowBack.setToX(1);

        stHideFront.setOnFinished(t -> stShowBack.play());

        Group group = new Group();
        group.getChildren().addAll(front,back);



        Scene flipScene = new Scene(group, 1080, 700);
        flipStage.setScene(flipScene);
        flipStage.setTitle("Animating Shuffle");
        flipStage.show();
        stHideFront.play();


    }
}

[10.10.22, 21:17:57] David Kn√∂rzer: 4.1) The fundamentals of ACID consistency are database rules. A consistent system will guarantee the uniqueness of a value across all operations if a schema specifies that it must be so. A consistent system will make sure the state can't contain linked rows once the base row is erased if a foreign key suggests deleting one row will delete related rows.
In a distributed system with several nodes, CAP consistency guarantees that each replica of the same logical item always has the same precise value. It should be noted that this is a logical assurance rather than a tangible one. Replicating values across a cluster might require some non-zero time due to the speed of light. By preventing clients from accessing different values at various nodes, the cluster can nevertheless display a logical view.
When systems provide more than just a basic key-value storage, these principles come together in an especially intriguing way. CAP consistency gets more complicated when systems give part or all the ACID features throughout a cluster. If a system provides repeating reads, compare-and-set, or full transactions, it must provide such assurances at every node to be CAP consistent. Therefore, these qualities are rarely guaranteed by systems that prioritize CAP availability over CAP consistency.
[10.10.22, 21:17:59] David Kn√∂rzer: das hani
[10.10.22, 21:18:12] Philipp Yanni: 1 ufgob hesch s√§lber gmacht
[10.10.22, 21:18:15] Philipp Yanni: du schmarotzer du
[10.10.22, 21:18:16] David Kn√∂rzer: 3.1) By requiring each node to maintain a finger table, Chord replaces the previous linear search with a quicker one. The distance, the target's hash ID, and the node responsible for that ID are all kept in each entry of the finger table. The finger table's first entry represents the node's direct successor (and therefore an extra successor field is not needed). Every time a node needs to look up a key, it passes the request to the nearest successor or predecessor (depending on the finger table) of k in its finger table (the "biggest" one on the circle whose ID is smaller than k), up until the node discovers the key is kept in its immediate successor. 
In an N-node network, this finger table reduces the number of nodes that must be consulted to locate a successor to O(log N).

[10.12.22, 18:04:51] David Kn√∂rzer: def get_modification_statistics(package, mod_type):
    """
    Returns modification statistics for the given package if it exists (uses the line_changes_per_package and aggregates the data from file-level to package-level, while keeping the data separate by author).
    Modification type can be passed to control which statistic should be returned.
    Returned data: dictionary "author email => statistic"
    """
    author_to_stat = defaultdict(int)
    if package not in line_changes_per_package:
        print(f'Package {package} not found.')
        return author_to_stat
    for author, files in line_changes_per_package[package].items():
        author_stat = author_to_stat.get(author, 0)
        for file, stat in files.items():
            if mod_type is Modification.ADDED:
                author_stat = author_stat + stat[0]
            elif mod_type is Modification.REMOVED:
                author_stat = author_stat + stat[1]
            elif mod_type is Modification.TOTAL:
                author_stat = author_stat + stat[0] + stat[1]
            elif mod_type is Modification.DIFF:
                author_stat = author_stat + stat[0] - stat[1]
            else:
                print(f'{mod_type} is an invalid modification type.')
                return author_to_stat
            author_to_stat[author] = author_stat
    return author_to_stat

# line_changes_per_package
